## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Stack Protection Mechanisms in LLVM

## Your Task

Find all C++ source files in `llvm/llvm-project` that implement stack protection mechanisms against buffer overflow attacks. Specifically identify: 1. The LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks (look for `StackProtector` in `llvm/lib/CodeGen/`). 2. The file that defines the `SafeStack` pass that separates safe and unsafe stack allocations (under `llvm/lib/CodeGen/`). 3. The header file that declares the stack protection pass interface. 4. The compiler-rt runtime file that provides the `__stack_chk_fail` implementation (look under `compiler-rt/lib/builtins/`). 5. Any file in `llvm/lib/Transforms/Instrumentation/` that implements memory safety instrumentation related to stack frame protection. Report the repo, file path, and the primary function or class handling stack protection for each.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the security domain.

## Available Resources

No local repositories are pre-checked out.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `github.com/llvm/llvm-project` (llvm/llvm-project)
- `github.com/gcc-mirror/gcc` (gcc-mirror/gcc)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the stack protection mechanisms in LLVM and created the answer file. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Stack Protection Mechanisms in LLVM

**5 Primary Files Identified:**

1. **StackProtector Pass** (`llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp`)
   - Main LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks
   - Classes: `StackProtectorPass`, `StackProtector` (legacy), `SSPLayoutAnalysis`
   - Key function: `InsertStackProtectors()` - inserts prologue code to load/store canary and epilogue code to verify it

2. **SafeStack Pass** (`llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp`)
   - Separates safe and unsafe stack allocations
   - Classes: `SafeStackPass`, `SafeStack` (main implementation), `SafeStackLegacyPass`
   - Key methods: `SafeStack::run()`, `moveStaticAllocasToUnsafeStack()`, `checkStackGuard()`

3. **Header Files**
   - `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h` - Declares StackProtector pass interface
   - `llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h` - Declares SafeStack pass interface

4. **SafeStack Layout** 
   - `llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.h` and `.cpp` - Manages stack frame layout with `StackLayout` class
   - Handles efficient object placement and coloring

5. **Runtime Implementation**
   - `libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp` - Implements `__stack_chk_fail()` and defines `__stack_chk_guard`
   - Called when canary is corrupted; writes error message to stderr and aborts

All findings have been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with complete details about repository locations, class/function names, and their roles in the stack protection architecture.

protection mechanisms in LLVM are implemented across multiple files in the llvm-project repository. The primary stack protection implementations are:\\n\\n### 1. StackProtector Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/StackProtector.cpp)\\nThe main LLVM pass that inserts stack protector checks into functions. This file contains:\\n- **StackProtectorPass**: The new PassInfoMixin-based pass class for use with the new PassManager\\n- **StackProtector**: The legacy FunctionPass class for backward compatibility\\n- **InsertStackProtectors()**: Core static function that performs the actual insertion of prologue code (which stores a random canary to the stack) and epilogue code (which checks if the canary has been modified and calls __stack_chk_fail if it has). The function generates code that stores a random value onto the stack before local variables are allocated and checks this value upon exiting, calling __stack_chk_fail if it has changed.\\n- **CreateFailBB()**: Creates a basic block for failure handling that invokes __stack_chk_fail\\n- **SSPLayoutAnalysis** and **SSPLayoutInfo**: Analysis pass and info class that determine which functions require stack protection based on buffer sizes, variable types, and function attributes\\n\\nKey methods:\\n- `PreservedAnalyses StackProtectorPass::run(Function &F, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM)`: New-style pass entry point\\n- `bool StackProtector::runOnFunction(Function &Fn)`: Legacy pass entry point\\n- The pass requires the LibcallLoweringInfo analysis to determine the appropriate runtime library calls to use\\n\\n### 2. SafeStack Pass (llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStack.cpp)\\nImplements the SafeStack pass that separates stack allocations into safe and unsafe stacks to prevent certain classes of buffer overflow attacks. This file contains:\\n- **SafeStackPass**: The new pass infrastructure class\\n- **SafeStack**: The main implementation class that performs the actual stack separation work\\n- **SafeStackLegacyPass**: The legacy FunctionPass wrapper\\n\\nKey methods in SafeStack class:\\n- `SafeStack::run()`: Main entry point that orchestrates the safe/unsafe stack separation\\n- `SafeStack::findInsts()`: Locates all static allocas, dynamic allocas, return instructions, and stack restore points\\n- `SafeStack::moveStaticAllocasToUnsafeStack()`: Allocates space for unsafe static allocas on the unsafe stack\\n- `SafeStack::moveDynamicAllocasToUnsafeStack()`: Replaces dynamic allocas with runtime allocation on the unsafe stack\\n- `SafeStack::checkStackGuard()`: Validates stack guard consistency and calls __stack_chk_fail if compromised\\n- `SafeStack::getStackGuard()`: Retrieves the current stack canary value\\n- `SafeStack::IsSafeStackAlloca()`: Determines whether an allocation is safe or requires unsafe stack separation\\n\\nThe SafeStack implementation splits the stack into two regions:\\n- **Safe Stack**: Regular stack for memory-safe accesses\\n- **Unsafe Stack**: Explicitly allocated and managed stack for unsafe access patterns\\n\\n### 3. Header Files\\n**llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/StackProtector.h** declares:\\n- `class SSPLayoutInfo`: Information about required stack protection layout for a function\\n- `class SSPLayoutAnalysis`: Analysis pass that determines stack protection requirements\\n- `class StackProtectorPass`: The new-style pass interface\\n\\n**llvm/include/llvm/CodeGen/SafeStack.h** declares:\\n- `class SafeStackPass`: New pass infrastructure interface with `run(Function &F, FunctionAnalysisManager &FAM)` method\\n\\n### 4. SafeStack Layout Classes\\n**llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.h** declares:\\n- `class StackLayout`: Computes the layout of unsafe stack frames, managing stack regions and object placement\\n\\n**llvm/lib/CodeGen/SafeStackLayout.cpp** implements:\\n- `StackLayout::addObject()`: Adds objects to the stack layout\\n- `StackLayout::layoutObject()`: Places objects in stack regions with proper alignment\\n- Stack region management for coloring and efficient space usage\\n\\n### 5. __stack_chk_fail Runtime Implementation\\n**libc/src/compiler/generic/__stack_chk_fail.cpp** provides:\\n- `void __stack_chk_fail(void)`: The runtime function called when a stack protector check fails.
